- [[primer-tm-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for the **base** test unit PRIMER-TM-001 (**Primer3 weighted per-primer penalty / objective function** — a *selection/scoring* algorithm, not a Tm calc, sibling of the dimer-Tm unit): Primer3 `libprimer3.cc` `p_obj_fn` (weighted sum of sign-gated one-sided deviations — Tm `temp_gt·(Tm−opt)`/`temp_lt·(opt−Tm)`, GC% `gc_content_gt/lt`, size `length_gt/lt`, plus `compl_any·self_any + compl_end·self_end + num_ns·#N`; **lower is better**, primers sorted ascending) + `libprimer3.h` (`DEFAULT_OPT_GC_PERCENT` undefined) + manual §19 + Untergasser 2012; defaults `opt_tm=60`/`opt_size=20`, weights `temp_*=length_*=1`, `gc/self/num_ns=0` ⇒ **default objective `|Tm−60|+|len−20|`**; oracles (60,20)→0.0, (63,20)→3.0, (57,18)→5.0, combined→8.0; sign-gated (at optimum term=0), weight-zero short-circuit, penalty≥0 (=0 iff all-optimal); `self_any`/`self_end` are caller-supplied `dpal` local-alignment scores (arithmetic exact, input external); no contradictions. Own concept [[primer3-weighted-penalty-objective]].
- [[primer-tm-001-hairpin-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit PRIMER-TM-001 (**intramolecular hairpin self-folding MFE + unimolecular hairpin Tm** — the hairpin/secondary-structure extension of the primer-Tm unit; same ntthal/`thal.c` engine as the dimer): SantaLucia & Hicks 2004 (Table 1 unified DNA NN ΔH°/ΔS° reused verbatim as `NnUnifiedParams` stem stacks + **Table 4 hairpin-loop ΔG°37 increments** 3→3.5…30→6.3, loop ΔH°=0 / loop ΔS°=−ΔG°37·1000/310.15, **unimolecular hairpin Tm Eq. 11 `Tm=ΔH°·1000/ΔS°−273.15` with NO `R·ln(C_T/x)` concentration term**, Jacobson-Stockmayer large-loop Eq. 7 coeff 2.44, steric floor loops <3 nt, supplementary triloop/tetraloop + closing-A·T +0.5 as opt-in caller increment) + SantaLucia 1998 NN cross-check + Vallone & Benight 1999 (hairpin Tm concentration-independent 0.5–260 µM); hand-derived oracles `GGGCTTTTGCCC` (4-bp GGGC stem, TTTT loop) → ΔH°=−25.8, ΔS°=−75.48486216346927, ΔG°37=−2.3883700000000054, **Tm=68.6404 °C**, `GGGCAAAAAGCCC` (5-nt loop, 3.3) → Tm≈71.585 °C, poly-A → no hairpin (null)/NaN; assumptions bimolecular init & terminal-A·T penalty excluded (unimolecular core, UNAFold-consistent); no contradictions. Enriches concept [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]].
- [[primer-tm-001-nn-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit PRIMER-TM-001 (**per-oligo nearest-neighbour salt-corrected design Tm**, opt-in — the core ΔH°/ΔS°→Tm path + salt corrections, same SantaLucia model as the dimer/hairpin siblings): SantaLucia & Hicks 2004 (Table 1 unified NN ΔH°/ΔS°, Tm Eq. 3 with x=1/4 symmetry factor, p.419 worked example **Tm 35.8 °C**, Na⁺ entropy Eq. 5 `0.368·(N/2)·ln[Na⁺]` valid 0.05–1.1 M / ≤16 bp, Tables 2 & 3 mismatch/dangling cross-check) + **Owczarzy 2004** monovalent quadratic 1/Tm correction `(4.29·f(GC)−3.95)·1e−5·ln[Na]+9.40e−6·(ln[Na])²` (non-linear over 69 mM–1.02 M) + **Owczarzy 2008** divalent Mg²⁺/dNTP 1/Tm correction (dNTP chelation Ka=3×10⁴, mixed-regime reparam, falls back to monovalent) + Biopython `DNA_NN4`/`DNA_IMM`/`DNA_DE`/`Tm_NN`/`salt_correction` methods 5–7 (verbatim transcription of Allawi/SantaLucia/Peyret + Bommarito 2000 primaries → `NnInternalMismatch`/`NnDanglingEnd`; complement-not-revcomp key convention mirrored in `CalculateNearestNeighborThermodynamicsMismatch`); oracles GCGCGC self x=1 Tm 35.0473, ATGCATGC x=4 Tm 30.4338, CGCGAATTCGCG 61.1452 (@1 M/0.5 µM), Owczarzy vs Eq.5 @50 mM Na, CGTGAC/GCGCTG T·G mismatch Tm −6.4061; assumptions default C_T=0.5 µM + N=2·(len−1); non-ACGT → null/NaN; no contradictions. Enriches concept [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]].
- [[primer-tm-001-special-loop-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit PRIMER-TM-001 (**bundled special tri/tetraloop hairpin bonus tables** — the sequence-specific loop stability bonuses ntthal adds to a length-3/4 hairpin loop, now applied inside `calc_hairpin`, completing the opt-in increment the hairpin sibling flagged): libprimer3 `triloop.dh/.ds` (**16** entries, 5-char key incl. closing pair, ΔH −1500/−2000 by closing-pair family, **all ΔS=0**) + `tetraloop.dh/.ds` (**76** entries, 6-char key → `NtthalHairpin.TetraloopTable`, e.g. CGAAAG ΔH=−1100 ΔS=0) + `thal.c` `calc_hairpin` (bonus **added** for loopSize==3/==4 via bsearch, key = full loop string incl. closing pair, ΔH cal/mol / ΔS cal/K/mol; loops.* size ΔS°, unimolecular `Tm=mh/(ms+(N/2−1)·saltCorr)−273.15`) + SantaLucia & Hicks 2004 Eqs. 8–9 (model source) + primer3-py 2.3.0 oracles (tetraloop CGAAAG `GGGGCGAAAGCCCC` Tm 85.0335 °C, triloop CGAAG `GGGCGAAGCCC` Tm 84.7061 °C, non-special TTTT `GGGCTTTTGCCC` Tm 69.3995 °C unchanged, homopolymer/short → structure_found=False); only 3/4-nt loops get a bonus, closing pair is part of the key, legacy `FindMostStableHairpin`+`loopBonusDeltaG37` path unchanged; assumptions none correctness-affecting (verbatim, machine-precision verified); no contradictions. Enriches concept [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]].
- [[probe-design-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit PROBE-DESIGN-001 (**TaqMan 5'-nuclease hydrolysis-probe design rules**, opt-in extension over the unchanged generic hybridization-probe designer; **first PROBE-\* unit**): Applied Biosystems / Thermo Fisher (rank 2, chemistry manufacturer) + PREMIER Biosoft (rank 3) + ScienceDirect "TaqMan" (5'-G quenching rationale) + IDT (corroborating) sources; the TaqMan-specific hard rules — **no G at the 5' end** (a 5'-G quenches the reporter *even after cleavage* → hard rule, not a soft penalty; `SelectTaqManStrand` moves to the antisense strand when unavoidable), **more Cs than Gs**, **no run of ≥4 consecutive Gs** (separate from the generic homopolymer cap), **GC 30–80%**, **length 18–22 nt** (default, `minLength`/`maxLength` parameterised), **probe Tm ≥ primer Tm + 10 °C** (caller-supplied primer Tm; probe Tm via the PRIMER-TM-001-validated salt-adjusted `81.5+16.6·log₁₀[Na⁺]+41·GC−600/N` formula, not a TaqMan-specific NN calc); oracles CCATCACCCTACATCACC passes-all (primerTm ≤ 39.35), GCATCACCCTACATCACC fails 5'-G, ACCCCGGGGACCCTACAT fails GGGG-run, C=1/G=9 fails more-G-than-C, 16-nt fails len<18, GC 100% fails, sense GTTAGGGTTAGGGTTAGG → RC CCTAACCCTAACCCTAAC strand-selection; two parameterisation assumptions (18–22 default window, repository salt-adjusted Tm engine), no source contradictions. Own concept [[taqman-probe-design-rules]].
- [[probe-design-001-lna-evidence]] — evidence artifact for the **LNA (locked nucleic acid) Tm-adjustment** variant of PROBE-DESIGN-001: an **LNA-adjusted nearest-neighbour Tm** that raises a probe's Tm/specificity (enabling shorter MGB-style 13–20 nt probes) by locking internal bases. Sources: **McTigue, Peterson & Kahn 2004** (*Biochemistry*, rank 1 — ΔΔH°/ΔΔS° increments for all **32** LNA+DNA:DNA nearest neighbours; internal LNA **raises Tm**), **MELTING 5** reference impl (`McTigue2004lockedmn.xml` verbatim table in **cal/mol** + `McTigue04LockedAcid.java` — **additive-increment** application and **terminal-LNA rejection**), rmelting worked example. Model: compute plain DNA NN ΔH°/ΔS° then **add** the McTigue increment per LNA-containing step, onto the library's SantaLucia-1998-unified DNA NN engine (same as PRIMER-TM-001 [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]]); terminal/non-ACGT/out-of-range → not-computable. Oracle CCATTGCTACC (LNA@4) → ΔH° −80.014 / ΔS° −216.6 → LNA Tm **63.528 °C** vs all-DNA 59.692 (**ΔTm +3.84 °C**), agreeing with MELTING `mct04` 63.614 to 0.086 °C (documented base-NN-set residual; increments applied exactly). Enriches [[taqman-probe-design-rules]] (LNA section).
- [[probe-valid-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit PROBE-VALID-001 (**hybridization-probe validation / off-target specificity scan** — a **gapped Smith–Waterman local alignment** of the candidate probe against a pooled reference, replacing an earlier ungapped Hamming scan; the **specificity-checking sibling** of PROBE-DESIGN-001, a genuinely distinct algorithm): Smith & Waterman 1981 (local-alignment recurrence with the **zero floor** → local, indel-aware; traceback stops at 0 so a mismatched tail is trimmed), Altschul et al. 1990/1997 BLAST (the **gapped-vs-ungapped** improvement — a single gapped alignment finds indel off-targets the ungapped HSPs miss; the unit realizes the *gapped local alignment* property, an **exact** full SW scan, not seed-and-extend or a genome-scale index), Karlin & Altschul 1990 / Altschul 1990 statistics (opt-in `ComputeLambdaNucleotide`/`ComputeKarlinAltschul`: `E=K·m·n·e^(−λS)`, λ = root of `Σ p_i p_j e^(λ s_ij)=1`, bit score `S'=(λS−ln K)/ln 2`, `E=m·n·2^(−S')`; preconditions expected-score<0 **and** a positive score; K caller-supplied), Kane et al. 2000 (empirical **>75% identity** cross-hybridization threshold, `minIdentity` default 0.75, caller-configurable; <14–15 contiguous-complement caveat); oracles — probe `ACGTACGTACGT` vs an indel copy `ACGTACTGTACGT` aligns `ACGTAC-GTACGT` 12/12 identity 1.0 `HasGaps=true` (**found by gapped, missed by ungapped Hamming maxMismatches=3**); indel+mismatch `ACGTACTGTACTT` → SW trims `TT` tail → 10/12 = 0.8333 (admitted @0.75, rejected @0.90); λ for +1/−3 uniform-0.25 = **1.3740631** (≈ blastn 1.37, expected score −2.0<0), K=0.711/S=30/m=20/n=1000 → bit **59.9627**, **E=1.7802e−14**, E↓ in S and linear in m·n; BLAST DNA scoring +2/−3 gap −2. ASSUMPTION: on-target = first perfect ungapped full-coverage exact match (API/labelling, not a sourced constant); no source contradictions. Own concept [[probe-offtarget-specificity-scan]].
- [[seq-atskew-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-ATSKEW-001 (**AT skew**, `(A − T)/(A + T)` — the A/T strand-asymmetry sibling of GC skew): Lobry 1996 *Mol Biol Evol* 13(5):660 (PMID 8676740, primary — founding intra-strand base-asymmetry observation over *E. coli*/*B. subtilis*/*H. influenzae*) + Charneski et al. 2011 *PLoS Genet* 7(9):e1002283 (verbatim formula; Firmicute AT skew from **selection not mutation**) + Wikipedia "GC skew" (both formulas + range **−1…+1**, AT skew `−1⇔A=0` / `+1⇔T=0`) + Biopython `Bio.SeqUtils.GC_skew` (symbol conventions — **case-insensitive** counting, **zero-denominator ⇒ 0.0**, ambiguous/non-canonical bases ignored); hand-derived oracles `AAAA→1.0`, `TTTT→−1.0`, `ATAT→0.0`, `AAAT→0.5`, `GGCC→0.0` (no A/T), `AAATGGGCCC→0.5` (G/C ignored), `aaat→0.5` (case-insensitive); corner cases empty/no-A-or-T ⇒ 0.0, non-A/T symbols ignored, bounds [−1,+1]; one documented ASSUMPTION (lowercase + non-ACGT handling inferred by analogy from the shipped `GC_skew` — formula itself fully sourced), no source contradictions. New family concept [[nucleotide-composition-skew]] (covers AT skew + its GC-skew sibling).
- [[seq-complex-compress-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-COMPLEX-COMPRESS-001 (**Lempel–Ziv (LZ76) compression-based sequence complexity** `c(S)` = number of distinct phrases in a left-to-right exhaustive-history parse): Lempel-Ziv 1976 (primary) + Wikipedia (definition + O(n) pointer-scan pseudocode) + Naereen reference impl (set-of-seen-substrings + 4 binary doctests) + entropy/AntroPy `lziv_complexity` (normalization `LZ_n = c/(n/log_b n)`, b = distinct symbols) + Zhang 2009 bio-sequence application; oracles raw **8/7/9/10** (Naereen), normalized **2.0** for `1001111011000010`, `"0"×16` raw **5** / normalized **1.25** (b<2 clamps log base to 2, returns normalized not raw — corrected from an earlier raw reading), `ACGT`→4, `AAAA`→2, empty→0; two ASSUMPTIONs (Naereen trailing-component convention, b<2 clamp), no source contradictions. New concept [[sequence-complexity-compression-lempel-ziv]].
- [[seq-complex-dust-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-COMPLEX-DUST-001 (**DUST triplet-frequency low-complexity score**, `score = ∑_t c(c−1)/2 / (L−2)` over nucleotide triplet counts; the DNA-sequence low-complexity **masker**): Morgulis, Gertz, Schäffer & Agarwala 2006 *J Comput Biol* 13(5):1028 (PMID 16796549, primary — "triplet frequencies in 64-base windows", SDUST rewrite = same score, symmetric/context-insensitive masking) + Li 2025 longdust arXiv:2509.07357 (verbatim score formula, `k=3` hardcoded, `L−2` = number of triplets, default window 64 / threshold 2.0 = level 20, **HIGH score ⇒ LOW complexity**) + lh3/sdust `sdust.c` (incremental `rw += cw[t]++` = closed-form `c(c−1)/2` sum, `if (rw*10 > L*T)` with `W=64`/`T=20` ⇒ score>2.0); hand-derived oracles `ATGC`→0.0 (all-distinct triplets) / `ACGTACGT`→0.333… / `AAAAAA`→1.5 / `ACACACAC`→1.0 / `AAAAAAAAAA`→3.5, homopolymer max `(L−3)/2`, `L<3` undefined; two ASSUMPTIONs (general `wordSize` normalization `L−w+1` — only k=3 source-backed; `L<wordSize`→0), no source contradictions. New concept [[dust-low-complexity-score]].
- [[seq-complex-kmer-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-COMPLEX-KMER-001 (**k-mer entropy** — Shannon entropy `H = −Σ pᵢ log₂ pᵢ` of the overlapping k-mer frequency distribution, `pᵢ = nᵢ/(L−k+1)`, bits; the **entropy member of the `SEQ-COMPLEX-*` family**, `SequenceComplexity.CalculateKmerEntropy`): Li 2025 longdust arXiv:2509.07357 (overlapping `L−k+1` k-mers, `H=−Σpᵢlog₂pᵢ`, skewed⇒low / uniform⇒high) + Çakır 2025 Entropy–Rank Ratio arXiv:2511.05300 (same formula, base-2⇒bits, single-nt max log₂4=2) + Shannon 1948 (bounds `0≤H≤log(k)`, deterministic⇒0 / uniform⇒log_b n); hand-derived oracles `ACGT` k=1→2.0 / `ACGT` k=2→log₂3≈1.5849625 / `ATATAT` k=2→0.9709505945 / `AAAA` k=2→0.0 / `AAACGT` k=2→1.9219280949 (=log₂5−0.4) / `AC` k=5→0.0 (L<k); homopolymer⇒H0, all-distinct⇒H log₂N; two API-shape ASSUMPTIONs (L<k→0; k<1→ArgumentOutOfRangeException, null DnaSequence→ArgumentNullException, null/empty string→0), no source contradictions. **Same formula as [[k-mer-statistics]]'s `Entropy` field** (a second entry point, not a new measure) — enriches that concept rather than adding a new one.
- [[seq-complex-window-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-COMPLEX-WINDOW-001 (**windowed sequence complexity** — a **sliding-window** scan emitting a per-position `ComplexityPoint` *profile*, each window carrying a **Shannon entropy** of base composition and a **linguistic complexity** value; the **profiling / scanning** member of the `SEQ-COMPLEX-*` family, distinct from the whole-sequence scalars LZ / DUST / k-entropy): Troyanskaya et al. 2002 *Bioinformatics* 18(5):679 (PMID 12050064, primary — **complexity profiles** as a function of position; linguistic complexity = distinct-subword counts, suffix-tree linear-time) + Wikipedia "Linguistic sequence complexity" (Gabrielian & Bolshoy 1999 / Trifonov 1990 — `Uᵢ = Vᵢ / min(4^i, N−i+1)`, summation `LC = Σ Vᵢ / Σ Vmax,i`, range 0<C<1) + Wikipedia "Shannon entropy" (Shannon 1948 — `H = −Σ p log₂ p` bits, uniform DNA max log₂4 = 2, deterministic ⇒ 0); hand-derived oracles `ACGTACGT` window → Shannon **2.0** / LC **23/29 = 0.7931…**, `AAAAAAAA` poly-A window → Shannon **0.0** / LC **6/29 = 0.2069…**, geometry L=24/w=8/s=8 → **3** windows ([0,7]c4 / [8,15]c12 / [16,23]c20); window count `floor((L−w)/s)+1` for L≥w else 0, only fully-contained windows emitted (no trailing partial), Position = `WindowStart + w/2`, bounds 0≤H≤2 / 0≤LC≤1; three ASSUMPTIONs (center-position label, default w=64/s=10, maxWordLength = min(6,w)), null→ArgumentNullException / w<1·s<1→ArgumentOutOfRangeException, no source contradictions. New concept [[windowed-sequence-complexity-profile]].
- [[seq-composition-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-COMPOSITION-001 (**sequence composition** — exact nucleotide counts/fractions A/T/G/C/U/N/Other partitioning Length, **GC content** `(G+C)/(A+T+G+C+U)`, and amino-acid residue counts; a **duplicate/consolidated Registry entry** over the two composition methods already delivered under SEQ-STATS-001, TestSpec §7): Biopython `Bio.SeqUtils.gc_fraction` (`gc/length` in **[0,1]**, empty ⇒ 0, case-insensitive `"CGScgs"`) + Wikipedia "GC skew" (GC/AT skew formulas, cumulative-skew origin/terminus) + IUPAC codes (canonical A/C/G/T/U + degenerate/N; the 20 amino-acid letters); worked oracles `ATGC`→GC 0.5, `GGGC`→GC 1.0/skew 0.5, `AAUUGGCC`→GC 0.5/AT skew 1.0, `MKVLWA`→6 residues each 1; corner cases empty/null ⇒ all-zero, no-G-or-C ⇒ skew 0.0, mixed case ⇒ case-insensitive, non-canonical letters routed to `CountN`/`CountOther`; one ASSUMPTION (degenerate IUPAC codes excluded from GC/AT totals — Biopython counts S toward GC / W toward denominator, agrees exactly over {A,T,G,C,U}), no source contradictions. New concept [[base-composition]]; skew members on the sibling [[nucleotide-composition-skew]].
- [[seq-dinuc-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-DINUC-001 (**Dinucleotide analysis** — dinucleotide frequency `f_XY = count/(N−1)`, the **Karlin genomic-signature odds ratio** `ρ_XY = f_XY/(f_X·f_Y)`, and codon frequencies; method `CalculateDinucleotideRatios`): Karlin PMC126251 (odds-ratio definition, `r=1.0` no-bias independence baseline, normalized frequencies) + Karlin & Burge 1995 via MBE 19(6):964 (interpretation thresholds `ρ≤0.78` under-/`ρ≥1.23` over-represented — documentation-only, method returns raw ratio) + Gardiner-Garden & Frommer 1987 (CpG O/E = same odds-ratio shape normalized by `N` not `N−1` → `N/(N−1)` modeling-choice difference) + Kazusa CUTG (codon frequency = count/total non-overlapping in-frame triplets, non-ACGT excluded); exact-rational oracles for `ATGCGCGT` (GC/CG ρ = 64/21 ≈ 3.0476, AT ρ = 32/7 ≈ 4.5714, TG/GT ρ = 32/21 ≈ 1.5238; f_XY GC=CG=2/7, AT=TG=GT=1/7) + codon `ATGATGAAA` f0→ATG 2/3/AAA 1/3, f1→TGA 1.0; div-by-zero guard (absent constituent base ⇒ expected 0 ⇒ ratio **0**), case-insensitive, null/empty/len<2→empty ratios, len<3→empty codons; two documented modeling choices (Karlin `(N−1)` vs Gardiner-Garden `(N)` normalization; `U` counted as a fifth base for RNA), no source contradictions. New concept [[dinucleotide-relative-abundance]]; CpG special case [[cpg-island-detection]]; codon-frequency metric shared with [[seq-codon-freq-001-evidence]].

- [[seq-entropy-profile-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-ENTROPY-PROFILE-001 (**sliding-window Shannon entropy profile** — per fixed-width window, `H = −Σ pᵢ log₂ pᵢ` bits over the window's **single-base (k=1) composition**; emitted as a standalone entropy profile). The **same per-window Shannon measure and window geometry** as the Shannon component of [[windowed-sequence-complexity-profile]] (SEQ-COMPLEX-WINDOW-001), just without the paired linguistic complexity → a **second entry point**, enriches that concept rather than adding a new one. Sources: Shannon 1948 *Bell Syst Tech J* 27(3):379 (primary, `H=−Σp log p`, `0·log0=0`) + Wikipedia "Entropy (information theory)" (base-2 ⇒ bits, uniform max `log_b n`) + IntechOpen ch. 75997 (DNA 4-letter alphabet, max 2 bits = log₂4, sliding counter of width W). Hand-derived per-window oracles `AAAA`→0.0 / `AATT`→1.0 / `ATGC`→2.0 / `AAAT`→0.8112781244591328 / `AATG`·`GCAA`→1.5 / `AAATTC`→1.4591479170272448; sliding profiles `AAATGC` w4 s1→[0.8112781244591328,1.5,2.0] / `AAATGCAA` w4 s2→[0.8112781244591328,2.0,1.5]; `windowSize>length`→empty profile, `==length`→single value, case-insensitive, bounds `0≤H≤log₂k≤2`. One ASSUMPTION (mono-symbol k=1 alphabet is the modelling choice — sources define H over any distribution; the k-mer/block generalization is the separate SEQ-COMPLEX-KMER-001 k-entropy on [[k-mer-statistics]]); no source contradictions. Enriches [[windowed-sequence-complexity-profile]].
- [[seq-gc-analysis-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-GC-ANALYSIS-001 (**Comprehensive GC analysis** — the composite `GcAnalysisResult` bundling whole-sequence scalars OverallGcContent `(G+C)/(A+T+G+C)×100` + OverallGcSkew `(G−C)/(G+C)` + OverallAtSkew `(A−T)/(A+T)` with a **sliding-window** GC%/GC-skew profile and the **population variance** `σ²=Σ(xᵢ−μ)²/N` of each windowed series). The overall scalars are already covered — GC content on [[base-composition]], GC/AT skew on [[nucleotide-composition-skew]]; the genuinely-distinct windowed profile + compositional variance → NEW concept [[windowed-gc-profile-and-variance]]. Sources: Wikipedia GC-content (Madigan & Martinko 2003 *Brock* `GC%=(G+C)/(A+T+G+C)×100%`) + Wikipedia GC skew (Lobry 1996 + Grigoriev 1998 cumulative-skew, spectrum −1…+1, sign switch = replication origin/terminus) + Biopython `Bio.SeqUtils` (`GC_skew` "multiple windows", zero-division ⇒ 0, ambiguous bases ignored; `gc_fraction` `[0,1]` = percentage ÷100) + Cuemath population variance (`σ²=Σ(xᵢ−μ)²/n`, worked `{12,13,12,14,19}`→6.8). Oracles `GGGCCAT`→GC% 71.428…/GC-skew 0.2/AT-skew 0.0; windowed `GGCC` w2s2→windows GG(+1,100)/CC(−1,100)→`GcSkewVariance` 1.0 / `GcContentVariance` 0.0; shorter-than-window ⇒ empty lists + variances 0, scalars still computed; no-G/C ⇒ skew 0/GC% 0. Two labelling/estimator ASSUMPTIONs (GC% ×100 vs Biopython `[0,1]` fraction; window "variability" = population variance ÷N, not sample ÷N−1), no source contradictions.
- [[seq-gc-profile-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-GC-PROFILE-001 (**sliding-window GC-content profile** — per fully-contained window, `GC% = (G+C)/(A+T+G+C)×100`, GC% only, no skew profile and no variance). Enriches [[windowed-gc-profile-and-variance]].
- [[seq-hydro-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-HYDRO-001 (**hydrophobicity analysis** — the whole-sequence **Kyte-Doolittle GRAVY index** `Σ(kd value)/length` and the **sliding-window hydropathy profile**, exactly `N−W+1` unweighted window means). Genuinely distinct SEQ-\* protein-property unit → NEW concept [[hydrophobicity-gravy-and-profile]] (the whole-sequence-scalar + raw-profile sibling that the segment-calling [[transmembrane-helix-prediction]] thresholds). Sources: Biopython `ProtParamData.py` kd scale (20 residues I 4.5…R −4.5, Kyte & Doolittle 1982) + `ProtParam.py` (`gravy()` = total/length, `protein_scale` loop `range(N−W+1)`, default `edge=1.0` = unweighted mean) + Expasy ProtParam (GRAVY = Σ hydropathy ÷ residues; positive ⇒ hydrophobic) + GCAT/Davidson (window 9 surface, window 19 transmembrane peaks > 1.6) + alakazam (CRAN) `gravy`. Hand-derived oracles `A`→1.8 / `AG`→0.7 / `FLIV`→3.825 / `RKDE`→−3.85; window-3 `FLIV`→[3.7, 4.1666666667], `AG` (W>N)→empty; case-insensitive, empty/null → 0/empty. One documented deviation (unknown residues **skipped** — GRAVY ÷ recognized count, profile treats as 0 — vs Biopython `gravy()` `KeyError`; neither mandated by the kd sources, in-alphabet values stay exactly source-conformant, algorithm doc §5.4); no source contradictions.

- [[seq-mw-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-MW-001 (**molecular weight calculation** — the average-isotopic **molecular mass in Daltons** of a **protein, DNA or RNA** sequence via one shared polymerization formula). Genuinely distinct SEQ-\* whole-sequence-scalar unit (mass, spanning all three molecule types) → NEW concept [[molecular-weight]], the mass-weighted sibling of the [[base-composition]] tally and of the [[hydrophobicity-gravy-and-profile]] GRAVY scalar. Formula fully sourced: Biopython `Bio.SeqUtils.molecular_weight` (`weight = Σ weight_table[x] − (len−1)·water`, one water removed per bond — peptide for protein, phosphodiester for nucleic acid; `water = 18.0153` avg / `18.010565` monoisotopic; single monomer ⇒ free-monomer mass, circular ⇒ −one more water, double-strand adds the complement strand, **error for protein**; "only unambiguous letters", nucleotides assumed 5'-phosphate) + Biopython `IUPACData` average tables ("from PubChem": protein *free-amino-acid* A 89.0932…G 75.0666…W 204.2252; DNA *monophosphate* A 331.2218/C 307.1971/G 347.2212/T 322.2085; RNA A 347.2212/C 323.1965/G 363.2206/U 324.1813) + Expasy Compute pI/Mw (protein Mw = "addition of average isotopic masses of amino acids ... and ... one water molecule", Da — algebraically = `Σ free-amino-acid − (len−1)·water`) + Expasy ProtParam (delegates to Compute pI/Mw) + Expasy FindMod (residue-mass table + H₂O 18.01524). Re-derived oracles (avg tables, water 18.0153) `AGC`→protein **249.29** / DNA **949.61** / RNA **997.61** (Biopython docstring), single monomer (zero bonds ⇒ free-monomer mass) `G`→**75.0666** / `A` DNA→**331.2218** / `A` RNA→**347.2212**; empty/null→0. One documented deviation (unknown/ambiguous symbols **skipped** — contribute no mass and no bond, reflecting only recognized monomers, no invented average — whereas Biopython *rejects* them; the SEQ-\* skip-unknown convention, an API-shape choice, in-alphabet values stay exactly source-conformant) + two API-shape assumptions (ToUpperInvariant case-fold; the skip resolution); no source contradictions (Expasy/Biopython agree on formula and average-mass tables to rounding). Note MW pairs with pI in the Expasy source but **pI/charge is a separate calculation not in this unit**.
- [[seq-pi-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-PI-001 (**isoelectric point (pI)** — the **pH at which a protein's net charge is zero**, found by bisecting the Henderson–Hasselbalch net-charge function over [0,14]). Genuinely distinct SEQ-\* protein-property scalar (a charge/pH calculation, not mass or hydropathy) → NEW concept [[isoelectric-point]], the ExPASy Compute pI/Mw partner of [[molecular-weight]]. Charge model fully sourced: Osorio et al. 2015 Peptides `charge_pI.cpp` (net charge `Σ_basic +1/(1+10^(pH−pKa)) + Σ_acidic −1/(1+10^(pKa−pH))`, Moore 1985; basic {R,K,H,N-term} / acidic {D,E,C,Y,C-term}, both termini once) + EMBOSS `iep` (pI = net-charge-zero pH, `Epk.dat` scale N-term 8.6/C-term 3.6/C 8.5/D 3.9/E 4.1/H 6.5/K 10.8/R 12.5/Y 10.1, [0,14] bracket, "no electrostatic interactions" ⇒ composition-only/order-independent) + Peptides `charge()` (nine pKa scales; EMBOSS worked example `FLPVLAGLTPSIVPKLVCLLTKKC` net charge 3.037398/2.914112/0.7184524 @ pH 5/7/9) + seqinr `computePI` + ExPASy Compute pI/Mw (Bjellqvist 1993 scale; small/highly-basic-protein accuracy caveat; pairs pI with Mw). Derived-pI oracles (EMBOSS, bisection ±0.01): `A`/`AG`→6.10 (termini-only midpoint), `D`→3.75, `K`→9.70, `DDDD`→3.23, `KKKK`→11.27, `FLPVLAGLTPSIVPKLVCLLTKKC`→9.67 (basic), `ACDEFGHIKLMNPQRSTVWY`→7.36 (EMBOSS ≠ seqinr Bjellqvist 6.78454 — scale-dependent). Two assumptions (empty/null→7.0 input-guard; pKa scale = EMBOSS, a parameter choice not a deviation), pI∈[0,14] invariant, no source contradictions.
- [[seq-secstruct-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-SECSTRUCT-001 (**protein secondary structure prediction** — the **Chou-Fasman (1974/1978) Pα/Pβ/Pt conformational propensities** evaluated as a generic **sliding-window mean-propensity profile**: for a window `W`, the arithmetic mean of each of the α-helix/β-sheet/β-turn propensities over each window). Genuinely distinct SEQ-\* protein-property unit → NEW concept [[protein-secondary-structure-chou-fasman]] (the conformational-propensity analogue of the [[hydrophobicity-gravy-and-profile]] hydropathy profile, sharing the exact `N−W+1` unweighted window-mean mechanism). Sources: Wikipedia Chou–Fasman (rank 4; nucleation rules 4-of-6-helix threshold 1.03 / 3-of-5-sheet 1.00 / turn ∏p_t cutoff 7.5e-3; ~50–60% Q3 / 29-protein caveat) + Kelley bioinfo lecture (rank 4; helix STEP 1–4 state machine, worked A 142/83 E 151/37) + CSB|SJU Jakubowski (rank 4; **Lys Pα 1.16**) + Przytycka NCBI lecture (rank 4; **Lys 1.14 0.74 1.01**) + ravihansa3000/ChouFasman reference impl (rank 3; full 20-residue Pa/Pb/Pt integer table, **Lys 114**) + BMC Bioinformatics PMC1780123 (rank 1, peer-reviewed; restates rules, helix ⟨Pα⟩>1.03 & >⟨Pβ⟩). Hand-derived oracles: single-residue window = that residue's tuple (A 1.42/0.83/0.66, E 1.51/0.37/0.74, V 1.06/1.70/0.50, N 0.67/0.89/1.56, K 1.14/0.74/1.01); `AE` W2 → helix 1.465 / sheet 0.60 / turn 0.70; `AEV` W3 → helix 1.330 / sheet 0.9666… / turn 0.6333…; `AXE` W3 averages only A+E; N−W+1 windows in N-terminus order, case-insensitive, W>N/non-positive/null/empty → empty. Three assumptions (the method under test is the generic **profile not** the nucleation/extension state machine, so default `W=7` is an API convenience not a CF constant; unknown residues **skip-and-excluded**; the **only contested value Lys Pα resolved to 1.14** — two independent sources incl. the reference impl vs a single 1.16), no contradictions on the 19 uncontested residues.
- [[seq-stats-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-STATS-001 (**the ORIGINAL sequence-composition umbrella** — nucleotide composition A/T/G/C/U/N/Other + Length, **GC content** `(G+C)/(A+T+G+C+U)`, **GC skew** `(G−C)/(G+C)` and **AT skew** `(A−T)/(A+T)`; also `SummarizeNucleotideSequence` aggregator + `CalculateAminoAcidComposition`). Connective tissue for the piecemeal-ingested composition family: [[seq-composition-001-evidence]] is a later duplicate/consolidated registry entry over the two composition methods first delivered here, [[seq-atskew-001-evidence]] split out the AT-skew member, and [[windowed-gc-profile-and-variance|SEQ-GC-ANALYSIS-001]] re-bundled both skews windowed. Sources: Biopython `gc_fraction`/`GC_skew` (rank 3; `gc/length`∈[0,1], empty⇒0, case-insensitive, `ZeroDivisionError`⇒skew 0.0) + Wikipedia "GC skew" (rank 4; both formulas, sign convention) + Lobry 1996 *MBE* 13(5):660 (rank 1, primary — intra-strand base asymmetry). Worked oracles `ATGC`→GC 0.5/skews 0, `GGGC`→GC 1.0/GC skew 0.5/AT skew 0, `AAAT`→GC 0.0/GC skew 0/AT skew 0.5, `GCCC`→GC skew −0.5, `AAUUGGCC`→GC 0.5/AT skew 1.0; empty⇒all-zero, zero-denominator skews⇒0.0, case-insensitive; one ASSUMPTION (degenerate IUPAC codes excluded from GC/AT totals — agrees with Biopython over {A,T,G,C,U}), no contradictions. **No new concept** — synthesized on existing [[base-composition]] (composition + GC content) and [[nucleotide-composition-skew]] (both skews).
- [[seq-summary-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-SUMMARY-001 (**`SummarizeNucleotideSequence` — the per-sequence summary record**: bundles Length, nucleotide Composition (A/T/G/C/U/N), **GcContent** `(G+C)/(A+T+G+C+U)`, **Shannon Entropy** `−Σpᵢlog₂pᵢ` bits, **linguistic Complexity**, and **MeltingTemperature** (Wallace len<14 / GC-Marmur-Doty len≥14) into one object). A **pure aggregation** — each field MUST equal its canonical per-metric method on the identical input, so **no new concept**: composition/GC → [[base-composition]], entropy → [[seq-entropy-profile-001-evidence]]/[[windowed-sequence-complexity-profile]], linguistic complexity → [[windowed-sequence-complexity-profile]], Tm → [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]] (legacy Wallace/Marmur default, SEQ-TM-001). Sources: Biopython `gc_fraction` + `MeltingTemp` (Wallace `4(G+C)+2(A+T)` / Marmur-Doty `69.3+0.41·%GC−650/N`) + Wikipedia Shannon (base-2⇒bits, max log₂n) + Wikipedia linguistic complexity (Trifonov 1990, `C=∏Uᵢ`, 0<C<1). Oracles `ATGCATGC`→GcContent 0.5/Entropy 2.0/Tm 24.0/Complexity 0.83968…, 16-mer `ATGCATGCATGCATGC`→Tm 43.375 (GC branch, len≥14); empty/null⇒zero summary, case-insensitive. One ASSUMPTION (Tm threshold len<14 = SEQ-TM-001 `WallaceMaxLength`, non-correctness-affecting for the summary's equality contract), no contradictions. **Corrects** the earlier "thin GC wrapper" description of `SummarizeNucleotideSequence` on [[base-composition]]/[[seq-stats-001-evidence]] — it is a full per-sequence statistics record.
- [[seq-thermo-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-THERMO-001 (**DNA duplex thermodynamics** — the full nearest-neighbor **ΔH°/ΔS°/ΔG°/Tm** 4-tuple of a Watson-Crick DNA duplex, a port of Biopython `Tm_NN` over the **DNA_NN3 / Allawi & SantaLucia 1997** table). Genuinely distinct SEQ-\* full-tuple thermodynamics engine → NEW concept [[dna-duplex-nearest-neighbor-thermodynamics]] (neither the legacy Wallace/Marmur scalar Tm nor the 2004-unified PCR-primer engine [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]]). Sources: Biopython `MeltingTemp.Tm_NN` (rank 3; DNA_NN3 table verbatim, two-terminus init counted off `seq[0]+seq[-1]`, `Tm=(1000·ΔH)/(ΔS+R·ln k)−273.15` with `k=(dnac1−dnac2/2)·1e−9`, default 25 nM each ⇒ k=C_T/4, salt method 5 `0.368·(len−1)·ln[Na]`, docstring `CGTTCCAAAGATGTGGGCATGAGCTTAC`→60.32 °C) + MELTING 5 User Guide (rank 3; Tm eq §4.2, F-factor 1/4 §4.3, default model "all97") + Wikipedia Nucleic acid thermodynamics (rank 4, cites SantaLucia 1998; per-terminus init corroboration). Oracles `GCGC`→ΔH −30.0/ΔS −84.91/ΔG −3.67/Tm −18.6, `ATCG`→ΔH −23.6/ΔS −71.81, length<2 ⇒ `(0,0,0,0)`, case-insensitive; zero correctness-affecting assumptions (only the length<2 API convention), no source contradictions.
- [[seq-tm-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-TM-001 (**`CalculateMeltingTemperature` — the standalone scalar melting temperature**, length-dispatched at `ThermoConstants.WallaceMaxLength = 14` between the **Wallace rule** `4(G+C)+2(A+T)` for short oligos and the **Marmur-Doty GC formula** `64.9+41·(GC−16.4)/N` for len≥14). A **%GC rule of thumb carrying no ΔH°/ΔS°/ΔG°** → NEW concept [[melting-temperature]] (the **third distinct Tm surface** and the canonical home of the Wallace/Marmur formulas, previously only sketched as the legacy default on [[primer-dimer-thermodynamics-tm]]). Sources: Biopython `MeltingTemp` `Tm_Wallace` (`4(G+C)+2(A+T)`, "rule of thumb 14–20 nt", `ACGTTGCAATGCCGTA`→48.0) + `Tm_GC` (general form `A+B·%GC−C/N+salt−D·%mismatch`; valueset-1 `69.3+0.41·%GC−650/N` Marmur-Doty, valueset-2 QuikChange `81.5+…−675/N`); the same evidence file's NN/`Tm_NN`/SantaLucia-1998 datasets belong to SEQ-THERMO-001. Oracles Wallace `ACGTTGCAATGCCGTA`→48.0 / `ATGCATGC`→24.0, Marmur-Doty `GCGCGCGCGCATATATATAT`→51.78 / 16-mer `ATGCATGCATGCATGC`→43.375; empty/null→0, case-insensitive. **Consolidation note:** SEQ-TM-001 is a duplicate/consolidated Registry entry over the two methods already delivered under SEQ-THERMO-001 (`CalculateMeltingTemperature` here + `CalculateThermodynamics` → [[dna-duplex-nearest-neighbor-thermodynamics]]) — consolidated not re-implemented (TestSpec §7). One ASSUMPTION (14-nt dispatch boundary, non-correctness-affecting under explicit flag) + NN-facet default C_T assumption + repo-vs-Biopython Marmur-Doty constant variant (64.9/−672.4 vs 69.3/−650); no source contradictions. Resolves the "SEQ-TM-001 remains un-ingested / natural home for Wallace/Marmur" follow-up flagged by the SEQ-SUMMARY-001 and SEQ-THERMO-001 ingests.
- [[seq-replication-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-REPLICATION-001 (**replication origin prediction via the cumulative GC-skew minimum** — the classic ori-finder: integrate an *integer* running skew (G:+1, C:−1, A/T:0, `Skew_0=0`, prefix indices `[0,n]`) and read origin off the global **minimum**, terminus off the **maximum**): Rosalind BA1F Minimum Skew Problem (rank 3, canonical worked example — 100-nt sample min −4 @ positions **53, 97**, re-derived in-session exactly) + Grigoriev 1998 *Nucleic Acids Res* 26(10):2286 (rank 1 — cumulative diagram min=origin/max=terminus, extrema ≈ half chromosome apart, leading strand G-rich) + Lobry 1996 (PMID 8676740 — skew sign flips at origin/terminus) + Wikipedia "GC skew" (max=terminal/min=origin); diagram oracles `CCGGGG`→`0,−1,−2,−1,0,+1,+2` (min −2 @2/max +2 @6), `GGGCCC`→`0,+1,+2,+3,+2,+1,0`, `AATT`→flat; `PredictedOrigin=53` first-minimizer tie-break; one documented ASSUMPTION — `IsSignificant` redefined threshold-free as `max>min` (invented `amplitude>count×0.01` constant **removed**), flat diagram ⇒ origin=terminus=0/false; no source contradictions. New concept [[replication-origin-cumulative-skew]] (the distinct cumulative-integration + argmin/argmax *locator*, vs the scalar/windowed skew).
- [[seq-rnacomp-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SEQ-RNACOMP-001 (**RNA-specific per-base complement** — `GetRnaComplementBase`, the IUPAC-complete RNA complement map; **RNACOMP ≠ composition**, this is complement chemistry, not the [[base-composition]] tally). **No new concept** — enriched [[rna-base-pairing]] (which already owns the RNA base complement `GetComplement`, RNA-PAIR-001): added a *SEQ-family full-IUPAC RNA complement* subsection. Same chemistry as `RnaSecondaryStructure.GetComplement` but IUPAC-complete (A→U/U→A/G→C/C→G, **T→A** treating DNA T as U; reciprocal R↔Y/M↔K/D↔H/B↔V; self-complementary W/S/X/N; non-IUPAC pass-through). RNA sibling of DNA `GetComplementBase` (SEQ-COMP-001, not yet ingested); distinct from DNA path (`GetRnaComplementBase('A')='U'` vs `GetComplementBase('A')='T'`). Sources: Biopython `IUPACData.py`/`Seq.py`/API docs (`ambiguous_rna_complement` = `ambiguous_dna_complement` with T→U; "any T is treated as a U") + bioinformatics.org SMS + NC-IUB 1984 (Cornish-Bowden 1985). One deviation: recognized bases returned **uppercase** (repo convention vs Biopython case-preserving) — casing only, complement identity unchanged; no source contradictions.
- [[splice-acceptor-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SPLICE-ACCEPTOR-001 (**acceptor / 3' splice site detection** — score candidate `AG` dinucleotides for the three cis-elements of a real 3'ss under the canonical **GU-AG rule**). First ingested member of the **splicing** family → NEW concept [[splice-acceptor-site-prediction]]. Three scoring surfaces: default `FindAcceptorSites` (**AcceptorPwm** PWM + PPT-quality, `(score/(count+1)+2)/4` [0,1] heuristic; weights from Shapiro & Senapathy 1987), opt-in `FindAcceptorBranchPoint` (18–40 nt window for the human **`yUnAy`** consensus, Gao 2008 conservation y@−3 0.790/U@−2 0.746/A@0 0.923/y@+1 0.751, found ≥ 0.8·3.210; Mercer 2015 corroboration), opt-in **MaxEntScan score3ss** `ScoreAcceptorMaxEnt` (Yeo & Burge 2004 23-nt max-entropy model; MIT-licensed maxentpy 82,560-record tables `Data/maxent_score3.txt`; canonical `ttccaaacgaacttttgtAGgga`→**2.89** cross-check, +8.19/−0.08); U12 **YCCAC** non-canonical scoring (Hall & Padgett 1994). Corner cases: < 20 nt → empty guard, no-AG → empty, cryptic intronic AG decoys, weak PPT skipped. All prior assumptions RESOLVED (PWM weights verified, normalization = design choice, branch-point constants source-traceable). Licence flag: bundled MaxEntScan table is the MIT port, not the academic-terms Burge-lab Perl. No source contradictions.
- [[splice-donor-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SPLICE-DONOR-001 (**donor / 5' splice site detection** — score candidate `GT/GU` dinucleotides for the almost-invariant `GU` intron start under the canonical **GU-AG rule**). Donor member of the **splicing** family → NEW concept [[splice-donor-site-prediction]] (5' partner of [[splice-acceptor-site-prediction]]). Single contiguous **`MAG|GURAGU`** consensus (−3..+6; 0-G/+1-U ~100%, −1-G ~80% for U1 snRNP; **no branch point / PPT** — asymmetric with the acceptor). Two surfaces only: default **IUPAC consensus match-fraction** `FindDonorSites`/`ScoreDonorSite` (plainer than the acceptor PWM+PPT; GC donors self-penalize via the +1-U mismatch 8/9<9/9, old 0.7 penalty removed), opt-in **MaxEntScan score5ss** `ScoreDonorMaxEnt` (Yeo & Burge 2004 9-nt window, **single 16,384-entry table, no overlapping sub-windows** vs score3's 82,560 records; canonical `cagGTAAGT`→**10.86**, +11.08/−0.12). GC-AG (~0.5–1%) + U12 **AT-AC**/`ATATCC` non-canonical donors. Corner cases: < 9 nt → empty, no GT/GU → empty, cryptic donors. All prior assumptions RESOLVED (PWM→IUPAC binary weights, normalization→match fraction, GC penalty removed). Licence flag: bundled MaxEntScan table is the MIT port, not the academic-terms Burge-lab Perl. No source contradictions.
- [[sv-breakpoint-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SV-BREAKPOINT-001 (**breakpoint detection from split / soft-clipped reads**). First ingested member of the **germline structural-variant (SV)** family → NEW concept [[breakpoint-detection-split-reads]]. Localize an SV breakpoint to a single base at the aligned/clipped **junction** of a split read: the SAM/BAM CIGAR **soft clip `S` consumes the read (SEQ) but not the reference** and sits only at a read end → **leading `S` = left / trailing `S` = right breakpoint** (ClipCrop "marginal point between clipped and matched sequence"; L/R-breakpoints; a no-`S` read = no signal). **Cluster** per-read junctions under three source-backed constraints — positional **tolerance** (ClipCrop "clustered within 5-base differences", 5 b), **minimum support** (SoftSearch ≥ x soft-clipped reads at a position, default 5 / configurable 2; support = # clipped reads in cluster), and **same clip-side + same chromosome** — with a **min clip length** filter (≤ 5 clipped bases dropped) and `RefineBreakpoint`. Repository `SplitRead` record: `PrimaryPosition` = anchored SAM POS / `SupplementaryPosition` = junction coordinate / `ClipLength`. Oracles: 3 reads @ 5000 ± ≤ 5 b, same chr, support ≥ 2 → one breakpoint ~5000; 1 isolated read → none; 5000 vs 5100 (gap > tolerance) → two below-support groups → none. Sources: SAM/BAM spec (samtools/hts-specs, rank 2 — CIGAR consume table / POS / S-at-ends) + Tattini-Magi 2015 review (rank 1 — anchored+imprecise split read, single-base resolution, clustering) + ClipCrop Suzuki 2011 (rank 1 — junction=breakpoint, 5-b clustering, L/R) + SoftSearch Hart 2013 (rank 1 — ≥ x clipped reads, orientation combining, min clip > 5). One ASSUMPTION (cluster reported coordinate = rounded **mean** of member junctions, sub-tolerance only, mirroring sibling `ClusterSplitReads`); operates on already-extracted `SplitRead` records, not raw BAM. Orthogonal to the oncology read-evidence [[gene-fusion-detection-read-evidence]] / [[chromothripsis-inference]]. No source contradictions.
- [[sv-cnv-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SV-CNV-001 (**read-depth copy-number variation detection**). The **read-depth-segmentation member of the germline structural-variant (SV) family** → NEW concept [[read-depth-cnv-segmentation]] (a distinct method from the split-read anchor [[breakpoint-detection-split-reads]] — aggregate **read depth of coverage**, not per-read junctions). Pipeline: **read depth ∝ copy number** (Yoon 2009) → **windowed counting** (non-overlapping fixed-size windows, one read per start position, per-window mean RD) → optional **GC correction** `r_i' = r_i·m/m_GC` → **log2 ratio** `log2(observed depth / reference depth)` (reference = overall median of window means when no baseline given) → **integer CN = round(2·2^log2)** (CNVkit "round" method, diploid ploidy 2) → **del/dup call** + segment merge (`DetectCNV`/`SegmentCopyNumber`). Diploid anchors (verbatim CNVkit): 0.5×→log2 −1.0→CN 1 (Deletion), 1.0×→0→CN 2 (Neutral), 1.5×→+0.585→CN 3 (Duplication/gain), 2.0×→+1.0→CN 4 (amp). Corner cases: **zero-depth window → no-call** (log2(0)=−∞ undefined, homozygous-deletion candidate, not −∞); **NaN log2 → Neutral (CN 2)**; CN clamped **≥ 0**. Sources: Yoon 2009 (Genome Res, rank 1 — RD∝CN, windowed counting, GC formula) + CNVkit `call.py` + calling docs (rank 3 — `n=ref_copies·2^log2`, anchors log2(1/2)=−1 / log2(3/2)=0.585, `max(0,ncopies)` clamp, `nan`→neutral). Two ASSUMPTIONs (reference baseline = overall median of non-zero window means; diploid ploidy 2), both source-supported. The oncology [[copy-number-alteration-classification]] (ONCO-CNA-001) is the classification layer *on top of* this same log2 ratio (swaps `round` for hard-threshold binning into 5 CNA states). Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[sv-detect-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SV-DETECT-001 (**structural-variant detection from paired-end mapping (PEM) signatures** — discordant read pairs). The **discordant-read-pair member of the germline structural-variant (SV) family** → NEW concept [[discordant-pair-sv-detection]] (a third read-evidence channel, orthogonal to the split-read anchor [[breakpoint-detection-split-reads]] and the depth-based [[read-depth-cnv-segmentation]]). Read how a mate pair's mapped **span + orientation** deviate from the concordant **FR** proper pair (SAM FLAG 0x02; **RF is everted/discordant**, not proper) and classify the SV type: span `> μ+c·σ` (FR, same chr) → **Deletion**, span `< μ−c·σ` → **Insertion**, **FF/RR** → **Inversion**, everted **RF** → **tandem Duplication**, mates on **different chromosomes** → **Translocation**. Span cutoff = `c` s.d. of the empirical insert-size distribution (BreakDancer `-c`, default 3 ⇒ mean=400/sd=50 ⇒ bounds [250,550]); **signature-then-cluster** with **min support** ≥ `-r` pairs (default 2). Corner cases: an insertion larger than the insert size is invisible to PEM span and its sequence is not recovered (split-read channel's job); below-support clusters dropped; cutoff bounds exact. One ASSUMPTION — inter-chromosomal (translocation) precedence evaluated **before** orientation (inversion defined only for intra-chromosomal flipped pairs). Sources: Medvedev/Stanciu/Brudno 2009 (Nat Methods, rank 1 — signature catalogue) + BreakDancer README + protocol (Chen 2009 / Fan 2014 — s.d. cutoff, min support, DEL/INS/INV/ITX/CTX codes) + SAM/BWA proper-pair FR convention (cureffi/FLAG 0x02) + DELLY 2012 / SVXplorer 2020 (orientation→type: RF=dup, FF/RR=inv). Consumes already-mapped read-pair records, not raw BAM; research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[trans-diff-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit TRANS-DIFF-001 (**two-group RNA-seq differential expression** — log2 fold change + Welch's t-test + Benjamini-Hochberg FDR). **First ingested unit of the Transcriptome / RNA-seq family** → NEW concept [[differential-expression]]. `TranscriptomeAnalyzer.CalculateFoldChange` / `FindDifferentiallyExpressed`: **log2FC** `log2((mean(treatment)+c)/(mean(control)+c))` (pseudocount c=1, positive = up in treatment, DESeq2 Love 2014 + Science Park lesson) + a **Welch unequal-variance t-test** raw p `t=(X̄₂−X̄₁)/√(s₁²/N₁+s₂²/N₂)`, unbiased (N−1) variances, Welch-Satterthwaite df, exact Student-t tail `p=I_{ν/(ν+t²)}(ν/2,½)` via regularized incomplete beta (Welch 1947) + **Benjamini-Hochberg FDR** reproducing R `p.adjust(method="BH")` `pmin(1,cummin(n/i·p[o]))[ro]` (BH 1995). DE ⇔ **two-criterion gate** `|log2FC| ≥ threshold (default 1.0) AND adjusted p < alpha (default 0.05)`. Oracles: UP `log2(41/11)=+1.8981204…` / DOWN −1.8981204… / FLAT 0; Welch {1,2,3} vs {7,8,9} → t=7.348469, ν=4, p=0.0018262607 (SciPy cross-check); BH raw (0.001,0.4,0.5,0.9) → adj (0.004,0.6667,0.6667,0.9). Corner cases: <2 replicates → p=1; se=0 → p=1 (equal means)/p=0 (unequal); zero mean → pseudocount. Three source-backed ASSUMPTIONs (pseudocount 1, <2-replicate p=1, se=0 conventions). A **simple two-group** estimator, **not** the full DESeq2 negative-binomial GLM. `alternative_to` the rank-sum [[significant-taxa-detection]] (no built-in FDR); DE gene lists feed [[pathway-enrichment-ora]]. Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[trans-expr-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit TRANS-EXPR-001 (**RNA-seq expression quantification** — TPM / FPKM / RPKM + quantile normalization). **Transcriptome / RNA-seq family** sibling of the anchor [[differential-expression]] → NEW concept [[expression-quantification]] (a distinct quantification/normalization method, upstream of the DE test). `TranscriptomeAnalyzer.CalculateTPM` / `CalculateFPKM` / `QuantileNormalize`: **TPM** `(X_i/l_i)/Σ(X_j/l_j)·10⁶` (length-normalize into RPK **then** rescale so each sample **sums to exactly 10⁶** — the invariant RPKM lacks; Wagner 2012, Zhao/Ye/Stanton 2020); **FPKM/RPKM** `X_i·10⁹/(l_i·N)` (per-kb + per-million-reads; RPKM≡FPKM formula; `TPM=FPKM/Σ FPKM·10⁶`); **quantile normalization** (Bolstad 2003 — sort each column, set each rank to the cross-column rank mean, re-place; **tied values get the mean of the rank means they'd span**). Oracles: TPM A(10,2000)/B(20,4000)/C(30,1000) → **(125000,125000,750000)** sum 10⁶; FPKM X=1000,l=2000,N=10⁶ → **500**; quantile C1=(5,2,3,4)/C2=(4,1,4,2)/C3=(3,4,6,8) → C2's two tied `4`s → **5.166…** (mean of top-two rank means 4.666…/5.666…). Corner cases: all-zero counts → TPM 0/0 undefined → emit 0; non-positive length/N → FPKM 0; empty → empty. Two source-backed ASSUMPTIONs (all-zero TPM → 0; effective length = annotated length). Classic count-normalization, **not** an effective-length fragment model (kallisto/salmon) or TMM/median-of-ratios size factors (edgeR/DESeq2). TPM/RPKM are within-sample relative measures — misused across samples (Zhao 2020). Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[trans-splice-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit TRANS-SPLICE-001 (**RNA-seq alternative / differential splicing** — event classification + Percent-Spliced-In / PSI). **Transcriptome / RNA-seq family** sibling of the anchor [[differential-expression]] → NEW concept [[alternative-splicing-psi]] (read-quantification of splicing usage — **distinct from** the genomic splice-site motif predictors [[splice-donor-site-prediction]] / [[splice-acceptor-site-prediction]] / [[gene-structure-prediction-intron-exon]]). `TranscriptomeAnalyzer.CalculatePSI` / `DetectAlternativeSplicing`: **PSI** `Ψ = I/(I+S)` (inclusion / (inclusion+exclusion) reads; Wang 2008, PMC3330053, SUPPA2) with opt-in **rMATS length-normalized** `ψ̂ = (I/lᵢ)/(I/lᵢ + S/lₛ)` (Shen 2014, effective isoform lengths) → default unnormalized, switches to rMATS when both lengths > 0; **ΔPSI** = splicing-level differential readout. **Five canonical AS classes** (Wang 2008 = rMATS codes): SkippedExon (SE), RetainedIntron (RI), AlternativeFivePrimeSS (A5SS, alternative **donor** = moving 3′/END boundary of upstream exon), AlternativeThreePrimeSS (A3SS, alternative **acceptor** = moving 5′/START boundary of downstream exon), MutuallyExclusiveExons (MXE); an event needs **≥2 isoforms** of one gene. Oracles: (I=80,S=20) → **0.80**; (80,20,lᵢ=200,lₛ=100) → **0.6666…**. Corner cases: **0/0 → NaN**, S=0 → PSI 1, I=0 → PSI 0, `0 ≤ PSI ≤ 1`, <2 isoforms → no event. Two source-backed ASSUMPTIONs (length normalization opt-in; forward strand / ascending coords). The splicing-level counterpart to the gene-level [[differential-expression]] — a gene can be differentially spliced without changing total expression. Read-count ratio + coordinate comparison, **not** the full rMATS/SUPPA2 replicate statistics. Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[splice-predict-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit SPLICE-PREDICT-001 (**gene structure prediction — intron/exon**), the **composite / umbrella** of the **splicing** family → NEW concept [[gene-structure-prediction-intron-exon]]. Assembles the two boundary detectors into a whole split-gene model: find donors (`GT/GU`) + acceptors (`AG`) → **pair** into introns under the **GT-AG rule** (Breathnach & Chambon 1981 `MAG|GURAGU` / `(Y)nNCAG|G`; Burge 1999 "each donor pairs with exactly one acceptor") bounded by `minIntronLength` (default 60) / `maxIntronLength` → **greedy non-overlapping** selection → exons = the gaps → **type** each exon (Initial/Internal/Terminal/Single, Gilbert 1978) + **phase** = `(Σ preceding exon lengths) mod 3` (Alberts 2002) → emit **spliced sequence** + **overall score** = mean of per-intron `(donor+acceptor)/2`, [0,1]. Datasets: D1 two-exon 153 nt → 1 intron/2 exons/70-nt spliced, D2 single-exon 50 nt → Single, D3 empty → 0/0. Corner cases: 30-bp introns excluded by default min=60, no sites → single-exon, DNA T≡U. All 4 assumptions RESOLVED (greedy=design decision, phase=trivial, overall-score=definition, **default branch-point 0.3 constant removed**). No source contradictions.
- [[variant-annot-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit VARIANT-ANNOT-001 (**variant annotation** — VEP-style functional consequence + Sequence-Ontology IMPACT). The **interpretation / annotation** member of the variant-analysis family → NEW concept [[variant-effect-annotation-vep]] (downstream of variant calling [[somatic-variant-calling-tumor-normal]], orthogonal to pathogenicity/tier classification). Ensembl **OverlapConsequence predicate system**: `Constants.pm` consequence→IMPACT→rank table (**IMPACT stored on the term, not computed**; frameshift HIGH / missense MODERATE / synonymous LOW / intron MODIFIER) + `VariationEffect.pm` peptide predicates; **most-severe = lowest rank** (McLaren 2016 "most specific term under any parent"). The coding engine **translates ref/alt codons** through [[genetic-code-translation]] (NCBI Standard code table 1) and compares peptides: `synonymous` (ref_pep==alt_pep, no `X`, not stop_retained) / `missense` (differ, same length; false if start_lost/stop_lost/stop_gained/partial_codon) / `stop_gained` (alt gains `*`) / `stop_lost` (ref loses `*`) / **`frameshift` purely length-based `|alt−ref| mod 3 ≠ 0`** / inframe ins-del (×3). Precedence stop_gained>missense, start_lost(rank 7)>coding-substitution. Oracles GAA→GTA missense/MODERATE · TTA→TTG synonymous/LOW · CAA→TAA stop_gained/HIGH · TAA→CAA stop_lost/HIGH · ATG→ATC start_lost/HIGH · AC→A frameshift · A→ATTT inframe_insertion. Sources McLaren 2016 (PMC4893825) + Ensembl Constants.pm/VariationEffect.pm (release/110) + NCBI gc.prt + Sequence Ontology (Eilbeck 2005). Two assumptions (Standard code table 1 only; single-codon SNV peptide comparison). Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[variant-call-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit VARIANT-CALL-001 (**variant calling** — SNP/insertion/deletion detection from a reference↔query alignment + transition/transversion + Ti/Tv). The **calling / detection** member of the variant-analysis family → NEW concept [[germline-variant-calling-snp-indel]] (**upstream of** annotation [[variant-effect-annotation-vep]]; the germline reference↔query counterpart of the oncology tumor-vs-normal caller [[somatic-variant-calling-tumor-normal]]). `CallVariantsFromAlignment` runs `SequenceAligner.GlobalAlign(reference,query)` and walks aligned columns: **SNP** (both bases differ), **Insertion** (`-`/base), **Deletion** (base/`-`), 0-based `Position` + `"-"` gap sentinel (in-memory model; VCF padding + 1-based POS only in serialized `ToVcfLines`). SNPs classified case-insensitively **Transition** (A↔G, C↔T) vs **Transversion** (A↔C/A↔T/G↔C/G↔T); **Ti/Tv = #Ti/#Tv**, undefined `#Tv=0` → **0** by convention; non-SNP → `Other`. Sources VCFv4.3 (samtools/hts-specs — REF/ALT/POS + padding-base grammar, §1.1 `G→A` SNP / `GTC→G` 2-base del / `GTC→GTCT` 1-base ins) + Danecek 2011 (VCF classes) + Tan 2015 (normalized ⟺ left-aligned+parsimonious) + Collins & Jukes 1994 (transitional bias, Ti rate > Tv rate). Three assumptions (gap-sentinel internal rep; indels **not** normalized → position-only implementation-dependence in repeats; Ti/Tv zero → 0). Alignment-based (single query vs reference), **not** a read-pileup genotype caller. Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[variant-indel-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit VARIANT-INDEL-001 (**indel detection** — `FindInsertions` / `FindDeletions`, the insertion/deletion facet of the aligned-column caller). **Enriches** (does not fork) the concept [[germline-variant-calling-snp-indel]] — the indel facet of the same VARIANT-CALL-001 caller, not a separate algorithm. `FindInsertions`/`FindDeletions` are **filters over `CallVariants`** returning only their class (insertion column `-`/base, deletion column base/`-`); a multi-base indel = **consecutive per-base indel columns**. Load-bearing claim = the **directional length invariant**: **insertion ⇒ ALT longer than REF** (VCF `C→CA`), **deletion ⇒ REF longer than ALT** (VCF `TC→T`); VCFv4.3 §1.1 `GTC→G,GTCT` shows both anchored at `G`. Normalization theory (Tan 2015 **normalized ⟺ left-aligned + parsimonious**; Algorithm 1 = suffix-then-prefix trimming) documents the ASM: the caller reports the indel at the `GlobalAlign` column with **no** normalization pass, so **position** is implementation-dependent in repeats/low-complexity only (PharmCAT `AATGA→A`@97740414 ⇒ `GATGA→G`@97740410, same count/type), **not** counts or types. Reference oracles: `ATGCAT`→`ATGTCAT` = 1-base insertion `T`; `ATGTCAT`→`ATGCAT` = 1-base deletion `T`; minimal_representation CFTR p.F508del `(7,117199646,CTT,-)→(...,ATCT,A)` + BRCA2 `(13,32914438,T,-)→(...,GT,G)` confirm deletion ⇒ len(REF)>len(ALT) + left-anchor padding. Three assumptions (gap-sentinel internal rep; indels not normalized → position-only in repeats; 0-based in-memory Position). Sources VCFv4.3 + Tan 2015 (PMID 25701572) + minimal_representation (Minikel) + PharmCAT. Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.
- [[variant-snp-001-evidence]] — evidence artifact for test unit VARIANT-SNP-001 (**SNP detection** — `FindSnps` / `FindSnpsDirect`, the single-nucleotide-substitution facet of the aligned-column caller). **Enriches** (does not fork) the concept [[germline-variant-calling-snp-indel]] — the SNP facet of the same VARIANT-CALL-001 caller, not a separate algorithm (mirrors how [[variant-indel-001-evidence]] folded in the indel facet). Two entry points, **substitution columns only** (no indels): **`FindSnps`** = alignment-based filter over the caller (keeps columns where both bases differ, `Type=SNP`); **`FindSnpsDirect`** = positional / **Hamming-style** — over two **equal-length** sequences it enumerates exactly the **Hamming-mismatch positions** (Acharya 2017, PMC5410656) and the SNP count equals the **Hamming distance**. Each SNP: `Position=i` (0-based mismatched index), `ReferenceAllele=ref[i]`, `AlternateAllele=query[i]`, `ref[i]≠query[i]` (**REF==ALT is not a variant**). Load-bearing scope claim = the **equal-length precondition**: `FindSnpsDirect` on unequal-length inputs compares only the **common prefix** `min(ref.Length,query.Length)` — the trailing region is indel territory (VARIANT-INDEL-001), never a SNP. Identical sequences → 0 SNPs (Hamming distance 0); comparison + Ti/Tv classification **case-insensitive** (VCFv4.3 REF alphabet A,C,G,T,N). Oracles: `ATGC`→`ATTC`={2} (G→T) · `AAAA`→`TGTA`={0,1,2} · VCFv4.3 §1.1 simple SNP `G→A`@14370. Two assumptions (unequal-length → common prefix; 0-based in-memory Position). Sources VCFv4.3 + Wikipedia/Futuyma Transversion + Acharya 2017 (PMC5410656, Hamming) + Collins & Jukes 1994 (transitional bias). Research-grade, not for clinical use. No source contradictions.

- [[validation-verdicts]] — CLEAN validation-verdict registry: one row per per-unit report that found **no defect** (reports that found one get their own `[[<unit>-report]]` page instead), each linking the unit to its concept + Stage A/B state; see [[validation-ledger]] / [[validation-protocol]].
